    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

        state: 'apple_oauth_state_9995a096-39a1-4469-861c-a8d3d3a82c73'

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer2993288069750921613">Newlyweds, Celestial and Roy, are the embodiment of both the American Dream and the New South. He is a young executive and she is artist on the brink of an exciting career. They are settling into the routine of their life together, when they are ripped apart by circumstances neither could have imagined. Roy is arrested and sentenced to twelve years for a crime Celestial kn</span>
  <span id="freeText2993288069750921613" style="display:none">Newlyweds, Celestial and Roy, are the embodiment of both the American Dream and the New South. He is a young executive and she is artist on the brink of an exciting career. They are settling into the routine of their life together, when they are ripped apart by circumstances neither could have imagined. Roy is arrested and sentenced to twelve years for a crime Celestial knows he didn’t commit. Though fiercely independent, Celestial finds herself bereft and unmoored, taking comfort in Andre, her childhood friend, and best man at their wedding. As Roy’s time in prison passes, she is unable to hold on to the love that has been her center. After five years, Roy’s conviction is suddenly overturned, and he returns to Atlanta ready to resume their life together.<br />This stirring love story is a deeply insightful look into the hearts and minds of three people who are at once bound and separated by forces beyond their control. An American Marriage is a masterpiece of storytelling, an intimate look into the souls of people who must reckon with the past while moving forward- with hope and pain- into the future.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2993288069750921613" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

It's about how tenuous relationships can be without adding what happened... it's wondering if the end was inevitable without the middle.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I would say that it's tragic because it shows life's injustice and the messiness of human relationships. However, it is not gratuitously melancholy li<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I would say that it's tragic because it shows life's injustice and the messiness of human relationships. However, it is not gratuitously melancholy like a lot of books--it's real and there's growth and hope.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>

<div id="review_2875339152" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2875339152" />
    <a title="Bill Gates" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/62787798-bill-gates"><img alt="Bill Gates" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603744542p2/62787798.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2875339152?book_show_action=true">Dec 12, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bill Gates" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bill Gates" href="/user/show/62787798-bill-gates">Bill Gates</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2875339152" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6218420806114543710">A couple years ago, Melinda and I visited a state prison in Georgia as part of our foundation’s work on U.S. poverty. I’d never been to a prison before, and it was an eye-opening experience.<br/><br/>The most memorable part was the discussion we had with some of the inmates about transitioning back into society. Although most were looking forward to leaving prison behind, some were clearly anxious about it. One man told us he was scared to re-enter society after so many years behind bars. Another mentione</span>
  <span id="freeText6218420806114543710" style="display:none">A couple years ago, Melinda and I visited a state prison in Georgia as part of our foundation’s work on U.S. poverty. I’d never been to a prison before, and it was an eye-opening experience.<br /><br />The most memorable part was the discussion we had with some of the inmates about transitioning back into society. Although most were looking forward to leaving prison behind, some were clearly anxious about it. One man told us he was scared to re-enter society after so many years behind bars. Another mentioned that it felt like he was a car about to be dropped into the middle of a racetrack where the other cars are already going 200 miles per hour.<br /><br />I couldn’t help but think about that conversation when I was reading <i>An American Marriage</i> by Tayari Jones. Although it’s fictional, the story is about the question at the heart of the anxiety Melinda and I saw that day: how do you rebuild your life after prison?<br /><br />Our daughter Jenn recommended that we read this deeply moving story about how one incident of injustice reshapes the lives of a black couple in the South and eventually dooms their relationship. Roy and Celestial are newlyweds living in Atlanta. They seemed to have it all: good careers, a decent house, and a lot of love for one another (although their marriage wasn’t perfect).<br /><br />That all changes when Roy gets falsely accused of rape and sentenced to 12 years in prison. Despite how radically this event changes their lives, Jones doesn’t spend much time on it. She devotes only five pages to Roy’s arrest and trial. Her message is clear: Roy is innocent, Celestial knows it, and neither fact matters. He’s caught up in the system regardless.<br /><br />What Jones is more interested in is how incarceration changes relationships. About half of the book is letters exchanged between Roy and Celestial while he’s locked up. Although they start out sweetly, the letters become more tense as time goes on. Eventually, Celestial stops writing to Roy altogether. By the time he gets released from prison seven years early, she’s moved on. (I promise this isn’t a spoiler. It’s in the book’s jacket description!)<br /><br />There’s this mythical notion that you’ll wait forever for the person you love. Penelope from the Odyssey is the classic example—she fights off potential suitors for 20 years waiting for her husband, Odysseus, to return from war.<br /><br />It’s a romantic idea, but is it realistic? Jones doesn’t seem to think so. We all like to imagine we’d be Penelope in that situation, but I suspect many would end up like Celestial instead. She writes to Roy, “You may feel like you’re carrying a burden, but I shoulder a load as well.” Later, she says, “A marriage is more than your heart, it’s your life. And we are not sharing ours.”<br /><br />The fact that their marriage didn’t have a fairytale ending felt realistic. Roy’s unjust incarceration—and the separation it caused—pushed on the seams that already existed in their relationship, and eventually those seams broke. Despite her decision to leave him, Celestial is a sympathetic character. You understand why she made her choice.<br /><br /><i>An American Marriage</i> is fundamentally a story about how incarceration hurts more than just the person locked up. It’s also a reminder of how draconian our criminal justice system can be—especially for black men like Roy. Once you get sucked into that system, you’re marked for life. Everything you were or had can disappear while you’re in prison.<br /><br />In a letter to his lawyer, Roy writes about how things have been difficult for Celestial but even more difficult for him. “I try to see her side of things, but it’s hard to weep for anyone who is out in the world living their dream,” he says.<br /><br />Jones is such a good writer that you can’t help but empathize with Roy and Celestial. Both have been put into a super-difficult position. I obviously haven’t experienced what they go through, but the characters—and their reactions to the situation—ring true to me.<br /><br />I wouldn’t say <i>An American Marriage</i> is a light, easy read, but it’s so well-written that you’ll find yourself sucked into it despite the heavy subject matter. If you’re looking for something thought-provoking to read this winter, you should add this one to your list.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6218420806114543710" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2241118691" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2241118691" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2241118691?book_show_action=true">Feb 22, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=modern-lit">modern-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=botm">botm</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2018">2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2241118691" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13261435570462218343"><blockquote>
  <i>Much of life is timing and circumstance, I see that now.</i>
</blockquote><br/>I know it's still early, but I've got a feeling <b>this is going to be one of my favourite reads of 2018</b>. It is a powerful, subtle, sad tale about the criminal justice system in America, and the personal, long-term consequences of its injustices.<br/><br/>There's a lot of discussion, articles and fiction looking at race-based injustice in the prison system of the United States. Most of these focus on racial-profiling of young black men, and how juri</span>
  <span id="freeText13261435570462218343" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>Much of life is timing and circumstance, I see that now.</i>
</blockquote><br />I know it's still early, but I've got a feeling <b>this is going to be one of my favourite reads of 2018</b>. It is a powerful, subtle, sad tale about the criminal justice system in America, and the personal, long-term consequences of its injustices.<br /><br />There's a lot of discussion, articles and fiction looking at race-based injustice in the prison system of the United States. Most of these focus on racial-profiling of young black men, and how juries are more likely to convict a black man than a white man when presented with the same evidence. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/33590210.An_American_Marriage" title="An American Marriage by Tayari Jones" rel="nofollow noopener">An American Marriage</a>, though, does something a bit different. <br /><br />While race - specifically, being a black American - is one of the major pillars of the novel, it is not so much the focus as the stage on which this tale of love, marriage and loyalty plays out. Instead of looking at the injustice itself, the novel turns to the far-reaching consequences of it - how lives are turned upside down and relationships fall apart as a result. It is <b>driven by complex and fascinating character drama</b>, moving between the perspectives of the entirely non-white cast to create a character portrait that is both broad and deep.<br /><br />Roy is a hard-working, entrepreneurial black man who has clawed his way out of a working-class background, earned a scholarship to college, and married a middle-class artist, Celestial. Next step: starting a family together. Then, during a trip back home to Louisiana, Roy is accused and convicted of a crime he didn't commit.<br /><br />As the first person narrative gives way to an epistolary format during Roy's time in prison, we see how Roy's incarceration drives a wedge between him and Celestial. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/33590210.An_American_Marriage" title="An American Marriage by Tayari Jones" rel="nofollow noopener">An American Marriage</a> asks us to consider what it really means to be married, and whether there comes a point when loyalty can no longer be expected. <br /><br />We are ultimately reminded that injustices against innocent black men are injustices against many others - the wives or husbands, the mothers and fathers, and the friends who love them. Jones sheds a haunting light on the all-encompassing nature of racial injustice. <b>It is extremely effective.</b><br /><br /><a href="http://thebookgeek.org" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/EmilyMayTheBookGeek" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="13261435570462218343" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2262273381" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2262273381" />
    <a title="Ashley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/62695678-ashley"><img alt="Ashley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1569797116p2/62695678.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2262273381?book_show_action=true">Feb 10, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ashley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ashley" href="/user/show/62695678-ashley">Ashley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/62695678-ashley?shelf=02-star">02-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/62695678-ashley?shelf=2018">2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/62695678-ashley?shelf=library">library</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2262273381" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13331479838513174934">2.5 stars<br/><br/>I know this book is getting a lot of buzz and it was Oprah's Book Club pick so I had really high hopes but it didn't really work for me. I started to give it 3 stars but after thinking more on it I just couldn't. For me, a 3-star rating means that overall I enjoyed the book. However, this book just didn't rise to that level. <br/><br/>I'll start with what I did like. I liked how the author weaved in the complexities of being a successful black American. Roy was a rising business executive but bec</span>
  <span id="freeText13331479838513174934" style="display:none">2.5 stars<br /><br />I know this book is getting a lot of buzz and it was Oprah's Book Club pick so I had really high hopes but it didn't really work for me. I started to give it 3 stars but after thinking more on it I just couldn't. For me, a 3-star rating means that overall I enjoyed the book. However, this book just didn't rise to that level. <br /><br />I'll start with what I did like. I liked how the author weaved in the complexities of being a successful black American. Roy was a rising business executive but because he was in the wrong place at the wrong time and fit a certain description his life/marriage was upended. The first part of the book is in epistolary form where we see the letter exchanges between Celestial and Roy while he was prison. In those letters you can see the slow changes in their relationship as time went on. This is basically the only part of the book where I felt any semblance of a connection to the story. <br /><br />Now for what I didn't like ... the characters. I didn't connect to Roy or Celestial so I didn't feel invested in their story. Also, I understand that life and marriages can be messy and that some decisions we make aren't always cut and dry. But some of the decisions that Celestial and Roy were making were nonsensical to me and not fully explained. Particularly in Celestial's case toward the end of the book. I didn't understand her. Maybe I'm missing something. <br /><br />Overall, I didn't have a strong emotional connection to the story. I'm sure many people will love this book but it wasn't for me. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13331479838513174934" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2338525113" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2338525113" />
    <a title="Meredith" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30978160-meredith"><img alt="Meredith" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1423329725p2/30978160.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2338525113?book_show_action=true">Mar 25, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Meredith" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Meredith" href="/user/show/30978160-meredith">Meredith</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/35064848-an-american-marriage">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2338525113" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15078668023964021046"><b>
  <i>I can’t say that I loved An American Marriage. What I can say, is that it made me think deeply about human nature, love, and, of course, marriage. <br/><br/>This is a thought-provoking, well-written, depth-filled character study about a marriage on the brink. </i>
</b><br/><br/>Celestial and Roy, a young couple from Atlanta, have been married for just over a year when Roy is arrested and sentenced to 12 years in jail. Will their marriage survive their separation or will they be able to withstand Roy’s incarceration? The</span>
  <span id="freeText15078668023964021046" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>I can’t say that I loved An American Marriage. What I can say, is that it made me think deeply about human nature, love, and, of course, marriage. <br /><br />This is a thought-provoking, well-written, depth-filled character study about a marriage on the brink. </i>
</b><br /><br />Celestial and Roy, a young couple from Atlanta, have been married for just over a year when Roy is arrested and sentenced to 12 years in jail. Will their marriage survive their separation or will they be able to withstand Roy’s incarceration? The bulk of the story focuses on a love triangle between Roy, Celestial, and Celestial’s childhood friend, Andre. In addition to romantic love and marriage, themes of motherhood and fatherhood, race, class, and tradition also play prominent roles. <br /><br />Told in alternating point of views, as well as through letters, the devolution of Roy and Celestial’s marriage is revealed through their letters. Some of the events are hard to read, and at times, made me a little uncomfortable. <br /><br />This is not a pretty read, nor is it one that is filled with action. What it does have are three very real, well-drawn out characters who are struggling with both the choices that they have made and not being able to change what they cannot control. I felt their pain, their emotions permeate the pages, and even though I didn’t always agree with them, I understood their choice(s). The ending felt authentic and while some might not like the way how things play out, I was satisfied. This is a credit to Jones who paints an honest picture of the characters and events that occur.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15078668023964021046" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2647903465" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2647903465" />
    <a title="chai ♡" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/42130592-chai"><img alt="chai ♡" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603167303p2/42130592.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2647903465?book_show_action=true">Mar 21, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="chai ♡" class="user" itemprop="url" name="chai ♡" href="/user/show/42130592-chai">chai ♡</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781786075192" href="/book/show/39699339-an-american-marriage">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=poc-rep">poc-rep</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=adult-contemporary">adult-contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=2018-releases">2018-releases</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=read-in-2019">read-in-2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=adult-lit">adult-lit</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2647903465" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1272867418700179122">This book stung so hard I almost looked for the cut of it on my skin.<br/><br/>It’s the kind of novel that sinks its teeth into you. One that enkindles in you such a brief and yet so excruciating pain. One that is so vivid the first glimpse of reality would shock you, and you would emerge from its thrall dazed, half dreaming, dizzy, and for a moment, aching, blinking, parched, unreal, everything else…fades away. One that changes you, leaves you a little different by the time you are done. But above all, o</span>
  <span id="freeText1272867418700179122" style="display:none">This book stung so hard I almost looked for the cut of it on my skin.<br /><br />It’s the kind of novel that sinks its teeth into you. One that enkindles in you such a brief and yet so excruciating pain. One that is so vivid the first glimpse of reality would shock you, and you would emerge from its thrall dazed, half dreaming, dizzy, and for a moment, aching, blinking, parched, unreal, everything else…fades away. One that changes you, leaves you a little different by the time you are done. But above all, one that reminds you that humans really are so often this way—inexplicable, restless, unyielding, and unfathomable.<br /><br />In sharp, vivid language that dwells on ugliness and beauty in equal measure, Jones explores, with soul-baring poignancy, the effects of a wrongful conviction on a young African-American couple in a haunting, compelling and deeply humane work of fiction. There are few novels so willing to give up their souls, but Jones’ sincerity sprinkles the text like sequins and her words are the skip of a stone across a lake, forming ripples and ripples of emotion.<br /><br />Being the victim of a wrongful conviction is one of those impossible things that happen in places so impossibly far away from where we are that they might as will not exist. But to Roy and Celestial, it came crashing down, as real as a reflection in the mirror.<br /><br />Roy and Celestial's life stretched out indescribably precious and sweet before them, with the years laid out ahead and the choices still there to be made: him as a rising corporate executive, and her building a portfolio as an artist. But Roy’s wrongful imprisonment was the rupture of the small, brave hope growing inside their marriage.<br /><br />Much of the story is told through the letters Roy and Celestial send each other during his incarceration. We witness as the fine grains of their relationship begin to course between their fingers. We watch as they try to cling on to a kernel of hope. But the years have stretched Celestial thin, leaving her waiting, trapped and trembling on the borders of her own life, and Roy’s life was getting white around the edges and sometimes, it seemed that he had no past, no memories, that he had been, for too long, on this stretch of tenebrous, hissing road. Neither could guess at the shape of an as-yet-uncharted future looming out of the fog. <br /><br />When Roy wins his release, it was all he had wanted to hear for five years. But freedom had never tasted so much like ashes. While Roy was despeteraly clinging to the hopeless longing for lost happiness, Celestial has begun forging a new life with her childhood best friend, Andre. Something has been lost in the long gulf of Roy and Celestial’s separation, and they don’t know whether they want it back or not.<br /><br />“<em>An American Marriage</em>” is a viscerally potent exploration of a difficult marriage that has tension and fraction stemming from good people trying their best, growing and changing and learning, and just as often, failing and screwing up or making the wrong choices. <strong>Two people, both crumpled and cast-aside, exhausted from their own efforts to become something more than a <em>consequence</em>, and who will always be married where it counted—in the horrors they had shared.</strong><br /><br />Jones lures you into Roy and Celestial’s lives only to do terrible, wonderful things to your head and heart. Reading this book, I was struck sometimes by the senseless idea that everything around me was made of glass. I was afraid to breathe, afraid to move. Dread lanced every moment, and my head was a spinning top of new and uncertain possibilities. I felt my heart limping in my chest as Celestial and Roy walked the floor of their relationship like tightrope performers, placing each foot gingerly in front of the other, testing for weaknesses, waiting for the moment when the whole thing eventually gives way.<br /><br />It would’ve been so easy to call sides—choose a character and place the weight of the blame on their shoulders. But Jones forces the reader to relentlessly ponder what Celestial and Roy really owe each other, as “<em>An American Marriage</em>” corkscrews into a tighter and tighter coil. With every page, we see various elements of the characters’ personalities which hitherto we had only glimpsed, but which had orchestrated and magnified themselves to a startling level of potency. Roy and Celestial—and even Andre—had made so many mistakes that they could not find their way back through their tangle to the first one. Roy had no words in their common language to explain that he is punctured and torn and needed someone to suture him back together, nor did Celestial, who felt herself wither a bit more inside way down deep where the light never reaches, and that might just be the final nail in the coffin they’ve been building between them.<br /><br />I felt torn in some way, grappled with the implications of the decisions the characters made. I wanted to step outside their heads and hope I would see from some new vantage something simple and understandable. But nothing about this story is supposed to be so stark, or so <em>simple</em>.<br /><br />A tight ache closed around my heart for Roy who’s been robbed of something he could never get back. Roy created a door between him and Celestial and he believed he could come back and knock and count on it being opened, and I couldn’t fault him for letting his mind lie to him because his world was more comfortable that way, because it hung together better that way. But I couldn’t fault Celestial for anything either. I couldn’t bring myself to resent the “<em>us</em>” that glimmered between her and Andre. Time is a funny thing—it doesn’t forgive the things that are beyond our control. And life is a river that cannot be called back once it leaves its banks. What had been taken from Celestial could never amount to what had been taken from Roy, but <b>is it selfishness to refuse to wait in an agony of wondering? Or is it selfishness to expect one to wait in the first place?</b><br /><br />Ultimately, this is what holds steady throughout the novel: <strong>Jones gives us a truth that is messy and nuanced, complex, and sometimes contradictory, and yields no easy answers.</strong><br /><br />At its core, “<em>An American Marriage</em>” is a love story, but reading this book, it's hard to escape its condemnation of a deeply flawed system of justice. "<em>What happened to me could happen to anybody</em>," Roy tells Andre who shoots back, "<em>You think I don't know that? I been black all my life.</em>" Roy might have survived a mordant injustice, but the shadow fell very dark on him. When justice was eventually served, it was a kind of escape, but it mocked <em>freedom</em>. It was not going to bring back Roy’s lost years. It was not going to change the past. But it will forever define it. Jones tells you that maybe it doesn’t have to define the future too. Roy's present might be overlaid with past sorrow, but he was free, and in the end, in that moment, that place, that perch upon the edge of the world, his view went on forever.<br /><br />I cannot recommend this book highly enough.<br /><br /><blockquote>☆ <a href="https://ko-fi.com/givemeabrekk" rel="nofollow noopener">ko-fi</a> ★ <a href="https://bookswithchaima.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">blog</a> ☆ <a href="https://twitter.com/givemeabrekk" rel="nofollow noopener">twitter</a> ★ <a href="https://azqaban.tumblr.com" rel="nofollow noopener">tumblr</a> ☆</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="1272867418700179122" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer3909316022732094308">Update: 2018 National Book Awards: Fiction <br/>Another great choice pick this year!!!<br/><br/><br/>SMALL UPDATE: I said I would come back and write a more complete review... but a few comments in here have inspired and encouraged me ... to perhaps leave this review alone. <br/>So.., I’ll only add a couple of things. <br/>Sharing First: it’s funny - what happens to our minds when we move on right away to reading other books after a deep thought- provoking read...<br/>It’s like ADDING more children to the family - expanding our h</span>
  <span id="freeText3909316022732094308" style="display:none">Update: 2018 National Book Awards: Fiction <br />Another great choice pick this year!!!<br /><br /><br />SMALL UPDATE: I said I would come back and write a more complete review... but a few comments in here have inspired and encouraged me ... to perhaps leave this review alone. <br />So.., I’ll only add a couple of things. <br />Sharing First: it’s funny - what happens to our minds when we move on right away to reading other books after a deep thought- provoking read...<br />It’s like ADDING more children to the family - expanding our heart to love and think about each one - differently- but each so special. <br />Recently it’s been like a grand slam rocking hot reading explosion experience.<br />It started with “The Weight of Ink” by Rachel Radish..(which I still think about)...<br />And THIS book...( which I still think about)<br />and now two others: “Fair and Tender Ladies” by Lee Smith <br />and<br />“The Gunners” by Rebecca Kauffman <br />BOTH of these two books I’m currently reading are EACH SOO GOOD - it’s a race to the finish line - as to which I’ll finish first... as I’m now so ‘deeply’ involved- in ecstasy reading both books (Listening to “The Gunners” during the day.. reading “Fair and Tender Ladies at night and middle of the night)<br /><br />My mind is swimming with wonderful feelings and thoughts and experiences of great created characters from our books <br />Little friends in our head.<br /><br />So... there are MANY VARIED REVIEWS on<br />“THE AMERICAN MARRIAGE”....<br />I’m only going to add one more final thought:<br />Opinion really! <br />I honestly believe there is something of great value in this book for: women- men- married or single - black - white - any nationality- all legal adult ages - young 20’s on up. <br />I mentioned in my little review that this book is a great ‘ examination of marriage...<br />I ALSO think it’s a great discussion whether or not to MARRY or NOT in this day and age. <br />There is ‘something’ ( no spoilers) - to pay close attention to at the beginning of this book... BEFORE MARRIAGE...<br />We’ve ALL had those experiences where our gut is warning us — something doesn’t feel right - our souls don’t feel secure &amp; safe—<br />but then as thinking beings— we’ve intellectualized the situation and let it go...<br />only later to kick ourselves for not taking the GUT MESSAGE more serious. <br />There was a ‘red flag’ moment in this story ..that I knew was going to come back to ‘haunt’ ... and it did. <br />My heart ached at that moment.<br />The ending of this book is also powerful - and in my opinion clearly sends a message.<br /><br />Not only had every character been broken— but culture conditions of injustice proved to be devastating too. EVERYONE WAS AFFECTED FROM THE HORRIFIC INJUSTICE...<br />but sadly - facing reality—<br />personal problems didn’t get swept under the rug. <br />Small problems didn’t get replaced with bigger ones. <br /><br />Brene Brown talks about learning to be comfortable with being uncomfortable. <br /><br />“The American Marriage” plays out those type of dialogues of communication. Characters were practicing being comfortable with very uncomfortable communication. <br />Truthful dialogue surfaced through letters. Later, face to face.<br /><br />Original... little review: <br />Phenomenal intimate gut-wrenching storytelling. Every character has been wounded. Their struggles are REAL. <br />Personally I had empathy for everyone— but I can understand if readers favor one character over another. There are complex uncomfortable situations throughout. <br />I could imagine how each person felt from their point of view. I felt those emotions, too.<br />This novel is definitely a ‘discussion’ book...<br />an examination of marriage: what happens when horrific circumstances literally change the direction of life? EVERYONE IS AFFECTED! <br />EVERYONE reacts differently! <br /><br />I’ve much admiration for the wisdom —the depths — of understanding that Jones has for all the many types of relationships we have in our lives. <br /><br />I need to get some sleep ...I’ll continue the rest of this review tomorrow or over the weekend.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3909316022732094308" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

I'd highly recommend for book clubs.<br/><br/>I’m afraid I’m in the outlier club with this one. <br/><br/>What I liked:<br/>-	The writing is gorgeous. 4-5 stars for the beauty of the prose.   <span id="freeText15101755351060515275" style="display:none">Edited 9/20 to add: My book club discussed this last night and while not everyone loved the book (but no one disliked it), it made for a lively and interesting discussion. I'd highly recommend for book clubs.<br /><br />I’m afraid I’m in the outlier club with this one. <br /><br />What I liked:<br />-	The writing is gorgeous. 4-5 stars for the beauty of the prose. Plus the author writes in a way that sounds like the way real people think and talk<br />-	The letters Celestial and Roy exchanged<br />-	How one unfortunate tragic event, unfair as it was, can totally change the trajectory of your life. It gives food for thought.<br />-	it was thought-provoking with complex moral themes surrounding loyalty and marriage<br /><br />What I didn’t like:<br />-	The characters. While I sympathized with their plight I just didn’t like them. Which I can’t explain because I usually like my characters somewhat complicated and flawed. Unlikability is not a deal breaker, but I like what I like and often I can’t even explain why I am so turned off by some characters.<br />-	The plot – after the beginning I just stopped caring. It felt like I was reading the script of a cheesy movie. There’s a time and place for cheesy, it just wasn’t what I was expecting when I went into this book.<br />-	The epilogue! My eyes may have rolled more than once. <br /><br />I will definitely read anything else the author writes because I found this book so well-written and her style so engaging, but this one just didn't quite work for me. It all boiled down to plot.</span>

<div id="review_2290718819" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2290718819" />
    <a title="Julie " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5210022-julie"><img alt="Julie " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1356906542p2/5210022.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2290718819?book_show_action=true">Feb 24, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Julie " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Julie " href="/user/show/5210022-julie">Julie </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5210022-julie?shelf=e-book">e-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5210022-julie?shelf=2018">2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5210022-julie?shelf=contemporary-fiction">contemporary-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5210022-julie?shelf=axis360">axis360</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5210022-julie?shelf=fiction-literature">fiction-literature</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2290718819" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer130602686271353401">An American Marriage by Tayari Jones is a 2018 Algonquin Books publication. <br/><br/>Well drawn characterizations and a thought provoking and timely topic combines to make a potent blend, which kept me riveted to the pages of this book. <br/><br/><br/>Roy had done everything right, is successful, married to a beautiful woman, living the American dream- until he is falsely accused of rape and sent to prison.<br/><br/>Celestial finds her comfortable life turned on its axis after Roy is incarcerated. She remains loyal to her husban</span>
  <span id="freeText130602686271353401" style="display:none">An American Marriage by Tayari Jones is a 2018 Algonquin Books publication. <br /><br />Well drawn characterizations and a thought provoking and timely topic combines to make a potent blend, which kept me riveted to the pages of this book. <br /><br /><br />Roy had done everything right, is successful, married to a beautiful woman, living the American dream- until he is falsely accused of rape and sent to prison.<br /><br />Celestial finds her comfortable life turned on its axis after Roy is incarcerated. She remains loyal to her husband, but as the years pass, her life continues to move forward, while Roy’s stagnates behind bars, and her feelings for him begin to wane, prompting her to seek comfort from another man.<br /><br />Meanwhile, lawyers are working round the clock to get Roy’s conviction overturned- which miraculously, after serving five years, it is!! <br /><br />But, Roy, soon learns that easing back into his former life and resuming his marriage with Celestial is easier said than done. <br /><br />What stands out for me in this novel, are the little nuances. Roy, who opens the dialogue in the first chapter, drew me in with his honesty, and humor, which was occasionally sheepish and self- deprecating, even though I disapproved of some of his actions. <br /><br />Celestial was, for some reason, a character I found difficult to warm up to at first, but upon reflection, I think her character may have gone through the most productive growth of all. <br /><br />Celestial’s needs and expectations are different from Roy’s ideals, some of which can be attributed to male/female roles and expectations in a marriage, and others to their own individuality. But, throw in a HUGE live altering test of the marriage and it will either strengthen or fall apart. Which way did things go for Roy and Celestial?<br /><br />The other timely topics explored have to do with racism and mass incarceration. Prison life is fraught with danger and loneliness, and of course Roy missed his former life, but it was simple things, things we so easily take for granted that makes the bleakness of his situation come alive. <br /><br />Despite their flaws, and each party has their fair share of them, they were basically ordinary people thrown in an extraordinary circumstance and left to cope with those circumstances as best they could. They were both human, with real needs, desires, hopes, and dreams. Both made excuses, both played the blame game, but both have a bond together they find hard to break free of. <br /><br />The epistolary parts of the novel were well done, which exposes both the closeness and the awkwardness of the marriage, but also the way time robbed them of the growth marriages need to survive. <br /><br />The secondary characters were added depth and conflict and were also very well drawn, and equally affected by the outcome of Roy and Celetial's marriage.<br /><br />While the book is not filled with action or suspense, or even, despite the heaviness of the situation, is it melodramatic, with one exception, that, to be honest, almost had to happen, to break the tension that boiled to the surface. There were a few tense moments that made me pretty uncomfortable, but mostly the author just allowed the characters to flow, to take charge, and dictate the pacing. This approach sounds understated and maybe even underwhelming, but this story was incredibly absorbing, and I have to say the conclusion was surprising- but at the same time- not. Despite some misgivings and mixed emotions about how the characters ended up, overall, I think they may be exactly where they need to be, both as individuals and as a couple. It may be tempting to take sides, but I can’t say I would do better or worse in that same situation, but I did struggle with passing judgments on occasion. <br /><br />Either way, this is a well written examination of relationships and human foibles, and how otherwise normal, well intentioned, good people face adversity and come out on the other end of it changed, for better or worse. <br />	<br />4 stars<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="130602686271353401" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2197969478?book_show_action=true">Feb 10, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brandice" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brandice" href="/user/show/36348070-brandice">Brandice</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36348070-brandice?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2197969478" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10371910373435090691">Is it possible that in mid-February I’ve already read my favorite book of 2018? <i>An American Marriage</i> was outstanding. Not only did I immediately become hooked and stay invested in the story, the quality of the writing was pure excellence. <br/><br/>A newlywed couple, Roy and Celestial, are early on in their marriage when Roy is sentenced to 12 years in jail for a crime he did not commit. This changes the course of their lives and feelings, and the story unfolds from here. Roy’s conviction is overturned 5 </span>
  <span id="freeText10371910373435090691" style="display:none">Is it possible that in mid-February I’ve already read my favorite book of 2018? <i>An American Marriage</i> was outstanding. Not only did I immediately become hooked and stay invested in the story, the quality of the writing was pure excellence. <br /><br />A newlywed couple, Roy and Celestial, are early on in their marriage when Roy is sentenced to 12 years in jail for a crime he did not commit. This changes the course of their lives and feelings, and the story unfolds from here. Roy’s conviction is overturned 5 years into his sentence too, changing things once again.<br /><br /><i>”But home isn’t where you land; home is where you launch. You can’t pick your home any more than you can choose your family. In poker, you get five cards. Three of them you can swap out, but two are yours to keep: family and native land.”</i><br /><br />There were different points in the book where I disliked all three of the primary characters, however I was so engrossed I had to keep reading to find out how this story would play out. I feel like there was excess in trying to frame Celestial as an independent woman though - Outside of a professional sense, I didn’t find her to be that independent at all. Her actions, to me, definitely indicated otherwise. I liked that while Roy and Celestial were both adults, their parents still played a central role in the story. I also enjoyed the many authentic Atlanta references throughout the book. <br /><br /><i>”But how you feel love and how you understand love are two different things. ... Human emotion is beyond comprehension, smooth and uninterrupted, like an orb made of blown glass.”</i><br /><br /><i>An American Marriage</i> portrays realistic behaviors and actions people experience, themselves and through others, and this is why I enjoyed it so immensely. While I just didn’t want it <i>to</i> end, I really liked the ending.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10371910373435090691" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2338975464" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2338975464" />
    <a title="Barry Pierce" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4593541-barry-pierce"><img alt="Barry Pierce" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588975731p2/4593541.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2338975464?book_show_action=true">Mar 25, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Barry Pierce" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Barry Pierce" href="/user/show/4593541-barry-pierce">Barry Pierce</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781616207601" href="/book/show/35746373-an-american-marriage">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4593541-barry-pierce?shelf=21st-century">21st-century</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4593541-barry-pierce?shelf=read-in-2018">read-in-2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2338975464" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2019174715204006283">I decided to pick up <i>An American Marriage</i> because Tayari Jones has a fun instagram. Also in her <i>By The Book</i> in the New York Times she recounts that she once accepted a gig in Dubai just because the flight gave her nineteen uninterrupted hours of reading time. I love that. She seems like such a fun and likeable person. Therefore it really does hurt to write that <i>An American Marriage</i> savagely disappointed me.<br/><br/>The novel concerns a married couple, Roy and Celestial, who live a fairly normal life unti</span>
  <span id="freeText2019174715204006283" style="display:none">I decided to pick up <i>An American Marriage</i> because Tayari Jones has a fun instagram. Also in her <i>By The Book</i> in the New York Times she recounts that she once accepted a gig in Dubai just because the flight gave her nineteen uninterrupted hours of reading time. I love that. She seems like such a fun and likeable person. Therefore it really does hurt to write that <i>An American Marriage</i> savagely disappointed me.<br /><br />The novel concerns a married couple, Roy and Celestial, who live a fairly normal life until Roy is sent to jail for allegedly raping another woman. Whilst in jail, Roy and Celestial try to keep the marriage going as normal but when Celestial experiences surprise success with her doll company everything between our couple begins to buckle and wane. <br /><br />I’ll begin with what I admired about this novel. I adore Jones’ turn of phrase. She has a very biting and almost sarcastic writing style which complements the plot well. Take this little sentence, which I loved, for example: <br /><br /><i>‘“Who are these men?” the white cop asked me. His accent was thick and gooey, all Marietta, turn left at the Big Chicken.’</i><br /><br />Isn’t that just wonderful? There’s little lines like that strewn throughout the novel like confetti.<br /><br />The novel is also very well structured. It employs three narrators, each rewarded a perspective, as the plot flows through their voices. Oftentimes I’m quite ‘meh’ about constantly changing perspectives but Jones makes it work flawlessly. She has a real master touch.<br /><br />However, no matter how much I polish it up, there’s no helping the plot of <i>An American Marriage</i>. Oprah recently chose this novel as her book club choice and, no offence to Oprah (I mean, she did get your aunt to read <i>Anna Karenina</i>) but this novel is <i>such</i> an Oprah Book Club pick.<br /><br />This novel reeks of <i>Lifetime</i> Original Movie. There are some moments that are just achingly sentimental whilst Jones often seeps into melodrama. The climax of the novel, a scene which I won’t spoil but tree huggers beware, was meant to be this great symbolic event in which every bottled emotion is finally unleashed. And I found myself… howling. Just howling at the utter ridiculousness of it. Talk about forcing a metaphor. Jeez.<br /><br />Thankfully this novel hasn’t put me off Tayari Jones. I’ve heard wonderful things about all of her other novels and I’m excited to get to them. But as for <i>An American Marriage</i>, I’m glad that Oprah saw something in it that I didn’t. That’s why I’m not Oprah. Even if I do share her devotion to bread.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2019174715204006283" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2303452285?book_show_action=true">Apr 19, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lindsay - Traveling Sisters Book Reviews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lindsay - Traveling Sisters Book Reviews" href="/user/show/54886546-lindsay---traveling-sisters-book-reviews">Lindsay - Traveling Sisters Book Reviews</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2303452285" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8206185445582390164">4 stars! This was a beautifully written, thought-provoking, slow burn novel that crept its way into my heart, settling deep within my bones. I will be thinking of these characters long after finishing this book.<br/><br/>This story follows Roy and Celestial, a young newlywed couple who have a passionate and impetuous relationship – loving deeply and arguing stubbornly. They are from different “worlds”, but have found an explosive love and connection with one another. Less than two years after getting marr</span>
  <span id="freeText8206185445582390164" style="display:none">4 stars! This was a beautifully written, thought-provoking, slow burn novel that crept its way into my heart, settling deep within my bones. I will be thinking of these characters long after finishing this book.<br /><br />This story follows Roy and Celestial, a young newlywed couple who have a passionate and impetuous relationship – loving deeply and arguing stubbornly. They are from different “worlds”, but have found an explosive love and connection with one another. Less than two years after getting married, Roy is arrested and sentenced to twelve years in prison for a crime Celestial knows he did not commit. <br /><br />The story is narrated by both Roy and Celestial, along with Celestial’s childhood friend Andre. There are several letters included throughout the story between various characters, mainly Roy and Celestial while he is in prison. These letters were a brilliant addition to the story – my connection with the characters grew stronger as each letter was revealed. <br /><br />The author, Tayari Jones, writes with such beauty and clarity. I was fully invested in this emotional and chaotic story, rooting for these characters to overcome their devastating situation. My heart has made a special spot for “Big Roy”, Roy’s father – he was an outstanding and unforgettable character – I simply adored him!<br /><br />I highly recommend this deep and touching book. It took a few chapters to pull me in, so be prepared for a slow burn that will gradually make its way into your soul.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8206185445582390164" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2001176187" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2001176187" />
    <a title="Diane S ☔" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4159922-diane-s"><img alt="Diane S ☔" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598402138p2/4159922.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2001176187?book_show_action=true">Jan 09, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Diane S ☔" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Diane S ☔" href="/user/show/4159922-diane-s">Diane S ☔</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2001176187" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3569201021822023932">Roy has done the best he could with the life he was given. Now married to Celestial, a young woman with dreams of her own, are traveling to meet his parents for the first time. The visit will prove less than successful, and a terrible miscarriage of Justice will occur that will detail their young lives and marriage.<br/><br/>These are characters to that one wants to root for, wants things to turn out well for them. Of course, life seldom works that way, things change, circumstances beyond ones control int</span>
  <span id="freeText3569201021822023932" style="display:none">Roy has done the best he could with the life he was given. Now married to Celestial, a young woman with dreams of her own, are traveling to meet his parents for the first time. The visit will prove less than successful, and a terrible miscarriage of Justice will occur that will detail their young lives and marriage.<br /><br />These are characters to that one wants to root for, wants things to turn out well for them. Of course, life seldom works that way, things change, circumstances beyond ones control interfere. A story where events shape a future, where a chance meeting changes a life, where the only bad guy is the Justice system, a system it is almost impossible to defeat. The high cost of incarceration, prisons full of young black men, many times not given a voice, not believed or railroaded by a system who believes the must be guilty. For Roy, his life will never be the same. He must fight to remember who he was, where he was and what he wanted in his life.<br /><br />This author does an amazing job detailing the crisis in a marriage that was interrupted by the system. Her writing is clear, concise, but pointed and sharp. The characters fully developed people with wants and needs of their own. The love of a family, a father who cares for a son that was not always his, and a young woman who must make a decision that will definitely her life going forward. Quite a book, quite a story.<br /><br />ARC from Edelweiss.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3569201021822023932" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2264458413" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2264458413" />
    <a title="Debbie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8665845-debbie"><img alt="Debbie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1334166735p2/8665845.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2264458413?book_show_action=true">Jan 19, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Debbie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Debbie" href="/user/show/8665845-debbie">Debbie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8665845-debbie?shelf=couple-love-and-hate">couple-love-and-hate</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8665845-debbie?shelf=best-reads-2012-through-2019">best-reads-2012-through-2019</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2264458413" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12399364290123942266"><b>One sock officially knocked off!!! (equals 4.5 rounded up up up!)</b><br/><br/>I look a little funny on my pogo stick (yes, this is a pogo stick kind of book) since I have just one sock on, but I have my reasons, really I do. The reason is that there was a slump for me in the middle of the story, so that one sock just held onto my foot like nobody’s business. But it was a short-lived slump, and the beginning and the end of the book are so insanely powerful, the other sock almost flew off my other foot. Since </span>
  <span id="freeText12399364290123942266" style="display:none"><b>One sock officially knocked off!!! (equals 4.5 rounded up up up!)</b><br /><br />I look a little funny on my pogo stick (yes, this is a pogo stick kind of book) since I have just one sock on, but I have my reasons, really I do. The reason is that there was a slump for me in the middle of the story, so that one sock just held onto my foot like nobody’s business. But it was a short-lived slump, and the beginning and the end of the book are so insanely powerful, the other sock almost flew off my other foot. Since I can’t ignore the slump—where there was a teensy dash of god and ghosts (my most un-favorite set of “gees”)—I have to bounce around on the pogo stick with just one foot al fresco. Fine by me.<br /><br />Okay, okay, enough about my stupid socks. No need to talk about feet, for god’s sake. The main point is I’m flying high on my pogo stick because this book is amazing! So much depth and emotion! I just finished and I must write this review immediately so I transfer my excitement to the page while it’s rip-roarin’ hot. <br /><br />Here is how I felt: hyper-happy, then a yawn (and the threat of a Complaint Board), then hyper-happy on steroids.<br /><br /><b>Hyper-happy.</b> OMG what a great beginning! My favorite part was a series of intense letters between the married couple, Roy and Celestial. Wow are the letters loaded. There is conflict, misunderstandings, gentle accusations. Each point of view is real and honest and argumentative. This is what I call psychological action. Each of them cornered, they say what they really think. There is blame yet no blame. No sugar coating.<br /><br /><b>What? I want more letters!</b> Where did they go? They left and took the juice with them. Yep, about halfway through, I started to yawn. This was the beginning of the slump that kept my one sock on, tight, and made me consider dragging out the Complaint Board. Why couldn’t the whole book be in letters? Even though I started out by getting attached to the characters, now I started feeling detached. And damn, I skidded on a patch of God, where it appeared in a whole short chapter, plus at the beginning of the next. Other scenes I didn’t like were a funeral and a visit to a graveyard. I know it’s just me, but I usually don’t like ceremonies—in books or in real life (unless something big and surprising happens). The ghost appears at the graveyard scene, where a dead mom gives advice: be a good man, blah blah blah. I thought that it was sort of clichéd. <br /> <br /><b>Hyper-happy on steroids!</b> Soon after the offending slump, I grabbed my pogo stick again. I wouldn’t think of pulling out the Complaint Board now. Hot damn! This is what I call high drama, and I loved it. It’s not melodramatic and it’s not over-the-top. It’s an incredibly realistic portrayal of marriage, a marriage that had to sustain a five-year separation. There is so much conflict, so much tension between the couple, I was riveted. This author gets into the heads of Roy and Celestial, and what we get is this tremendously insightful psychological story about the strength of love, guilt, expectations, disconnects. The author does an amazing job in making you empathize with Roy and his situation. He is flawed, however, and you don’t always accept his choices or actions—but you still love him. <br /><br />The dialogue is some of the most realistic I’ve read, and the story is as much about what isn’t uttered as about what is. It’s sharp, edgy, and honest. It has to do with illusions and delusions and hope and loyalty. It raises questions about relationships and morality. We know, for instance, that the reason for the separation, and what happened during that time, is no one’s fault. Feelings develop, feelings change—at least for some. Time changes things whether we like it or not. What is love and can people move on? Should you act on feelings when you know you shouldn’t? Do you stick it out when you really don’t want to? Can hope be powerful enough to get you what you want? It’s so much about the nuances of love and about how being apart can change things majorly. <br /><br />I don’t want to say anything about the plot, even about the big event at the beginning of the book that changes the course of Celestial’s and Roy’s life. I just love going into things cold, so that everything is a surprise. To me, that’s part of the fun of reading. Oh, I will say that I’ve read a few too many thrillers recently, because at the beginning I thought what was going on was sinister. Ha! No! Far from it! The book shows the severe consequences of social injustice (the cast is African-American) but it is in no way a message book.<br /><br />I always love it when a character does something you don’t expect. And that’s what is so cool about this book. When Roy returns after five years, I had absolutely no idea what was going to happen, and I loved every single surprise in behavior. There was this edge, this fear, although I kept telling myself that nothing bad would actually happen. Or would it? I must say I was so attached to both characters by that time. I felt like I knew them really well, yet they kept acting in ways I wasn’t expecting. Much wringing of my hands, but I was rooting for them both, bigtime. The dilemma they faced seemed to have no possible good resolution. My eyes did not leave the pages for hours. The way the book ends is brilliant.<br /><br />I must say, too, that the writing is fantastic. There are little bits of wisdom throughout. Here is a sample of her wonderful words:<br /><br /><i>“She was no bigger than a minute, so I bent my back to sweep her feet up off the porch and she laughed musical like a xylophone.”<br /><br />“Somehow she rearranges the ions in the air and you can’t breathe as well.”<br /><br />“In poker, you get five cards. Three of them you can swap out, but two are yours to keep: family and native land.”<br /><br />“His laughter broke whatever sticky spell bound us to the house, and we were able to leave.”<br /><br />“It’s like the difference between a raw egg and a scrambled egg. It’s the same thing, but it’s not the same at all.”<br /><br />“It’s like eating a butterscotch still sealed in the wrapper.”<br /><br />“Even while she wore his ring, she wasn’t his wife. She was merely a married woman.”<br /><br />“The secrets blocked my throat like a tumor.”</i><br /><br />I just remembered that long ago I read another novel by Jones, called <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9749711.Silver_Sparrow" title="Silver Sparrow by Tayari Jones" rel="nofollow noopener">Silver Sparrow</a>. Ann Patchett recommended it, and since I was enamored with Patchett’s <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9118135.State_of_Wonder" title="State of Wonder by Ann Patchett" rel="nofollow noopener">State of Wonder</a>, I jumped to read any book she dangled in front of my face. I remember that I liked Silver Sparrow and was super impressed by the writing, but I couldn’t tell you what it’s about. An American Marriage, on the other hand, will stick with me, I’m sure.<br /><br />I’m still hopping inside, hyper-happy, pretty manic. I was skeptical about reading this book, since it’s an Oprah selection and thus will be a big seller. (Big sellers are often a letdown.) I’m SO glad I didn’t miss this one. The characters are complex, their relationship is messy, and the story is profound. Now let me continue down the road on my pogo stick, the other sock threatening to fly off…</span>
  <a data-text-id="12399364290123942266" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer1468625817435646464">If somehow you have made it to July 2020 without being convinced that we need to burn the entire American justice system down and try again - go ahead and give this book a try.<br/><br/>Come back when you’re finished.<br/><br/>Okay, now that we’re all on the same page, literally and figuratively:<br/><br/>This book is so f*cking hard to read. It’s painful. It’s hard to like any of these characters, or dislike them, for that matter.<br/><br/>They are right and wrong and hurting and hurt and overall so goddamn human. It kills.<br/><br/>This story</span>
  <span id="freeText1468625817435646464" style="display:none">If somehow you have made it to July 2020 without being convinced that we need to burn the entire American justice system down and try again - go ahead and give this book a try.<br /><br />Come back when you’re finished.<br /><br />Okay, now that we’re all on the same page, literally and figuratively:<br /><br />This book is so f*cking hard to read. It’s painful. It’s hard to like any of these characters, or dislike them, for that matter.<br /><br />They are right and wrong and hurting and hurt and overall so goddamn human. It kills.<br /><br />This story is a necessary reminder that when we call innocent people guilty they are branded with the consequences of that guilt.<br /><br />When our justice system messes up, it messes up forever.<br /><br />And it disproportionately destroys the lives of Black Americans.<br /><br />Black people are disproportionately wrongfully convicted, disproportionately executed for crimes, disproportionately kept in prison and for longer sentences and for lesser crimes. <br /><br />If you are a fiction lover above all else, read this book, if it’ll help drive any of that home. <br /><br />And then read Just Mercy. Read nonfiction as well as fiction. Donate and march. If you are white, use your privilege for good, for once.<br /><br />This needs to end.<br /><br />Bottom line: We should aspire to live in a country where stories like this one are just that. Fiction.<br /><br />------------<br /><i>pre-review</i><br /><br />if you're in the market for a reminder that life is complicated and imperfect and there's no such thing as "the right thing" and we are doomed to hurt everyone we love...<br /><br />may i recommend this book?<br /><br />review to come / 3.5 stars<br /><br />------------<br /><br />reading this book about a man falsely imprisoned for a crime he didn't commit as part of my "Burn Down the American Justice System and Try Again" series<br /><br />---<br /><br /><i>i am spending this month reading books by Black authors. please join me!</i><br /><br />book 1: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2953004100?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">The Stars and the Blackness Between Them</a><br />book 2: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3372388250?type=review#rating_290994509" rel="nofollow noopener">Homegoing</a><br />book 3: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2718387154?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">Let's Talk about Love</a><br />book 4: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3090142486?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">Why I'm No Longer Talking to White People about Race</a><br />book 5: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3227618881?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">The Sellout</a><br />book 6: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3372395187?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">Queenie</a><br />book 7: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3372400231?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">Red at the Bone</a><br />book 8: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2586355320?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">The Weight of the Stars</a><br />book 9: An American Marriage</span>
